The Responsibility and Future of the Chinese Academic Society 177

— He Bingsong

Our country lags behind in everything, including academic research. Academic research is the foundation for the progress of all undertakings, so we must catch up quickly. However, we must not only discuss the old knowledge to make it more precise, but also cultivate new knowledge to make it more profound. The work is complex, and the responsibility is heavy. We want to seek the independence of Chinese academics and contribute to the progress of human civilization. It is imperative to unite comrades across the country and work together to succeed. If we use this meaning to evaluate our Chinese Academic Society, then we cannot help but admire the correctness and breadth of vision of the group of people who organized the society two decades ago. Now, the society has existed gloriously for twenty years. In these twenty years, the society, with the combined efforts of all members, has published more than one hundred special works and more than one hundred and fifty magazines. Although this achievement is not surprising, it is indeed worth our commemoration. Over the past twenty years, those who have presided over the society's affairs, those who have maintained the society, and all the more than nine hundred members have spent countless energy and effort to build the society into its current important academic position. We should pay tribute to them with gratitude.

In recent years, it seems that some members of the society feel that the society's business is limited to research and publication, and the scope is too narrow. They want to strive to contribute to practical undertakings, expressing the society's enthusiasm for serving the country and society. This spirit of service is certainly admirable. Especially at this time of national hardship, all our members should remember to catch up and do their best to promote the movement to revitalize the nation.

However, in my humble opinion, academic groups should not rush for quick success. It seems that academic research should still be its most important task. When we have spare energy, we may as well incidentally handle some undertakings that are directly beneficial to society, but we must never despise or even sacrifice our primary task because of this.

In fact, all construction undertakings in modern civilized countries cannot be separated from academic research as their prerequisite and basis. For example, the Soviet Union's Five-Year Plan and the United States' New Deal are all crystallizations of the research experience of experts in various disciplines in those countries, and they are implemented by the government. Recently, the most important point in the reform of the administrative structure by the Japanese military is the strengthening and expansion of the central research institutions. All this is enough to prove the importance of academic research in the construction of modern countries and societies.

Our Chinese Academic Society has a glorious history of twenty years, and we have more than nine hundred experts in various disciplines as our members. Moreover, we have successively published more than one hundred special works and more than one hundred and fifty magazines, and the foundation is extremely solid. We should adhere to the original intention of the founders and the original intention of those who maintain the society, continue to shoulder the responsibilities that academic groups should bear, and jointly make our greatest efforts in academic research.

If our original series of books can continue to be published continuously, and their content can be improved; if our original academic journals can increase the number of issues and pages in quantity and enrich the categories and content in quality, then we can not only tell the founders and the maintainers of the society that we are not guilty, but also give a satisfactory account to all members and the people of the country. In short, in my humble opinion, if we want to promote and carry forward our Chinese Academic Society, we should continue our spirit of hard research and continue to contribute our research results to the society as a gift from the society to our country and nation. Based on the past enthusiasm of all members for caring for the society, the future of our Chinese Academic Society is boundless, and that can be predicted. Let us all shout three cheers for the Chinese Academic Society!

The Chinese Academic Society in the Past Twenty Years 178

— Fu Biao

The Chinese Academic Society (hereinafter referred to as "this Society") was founded in the fifth year of the Republic of China by Chen Qixiu, Wang Zhaorong and other forty-seven students studying in Japan, with the aim of studying truth, promoting academics, exchanging knowledge, and promoting culture. Because the year was Bingchen, it was named Bingchen Academic Society. It was established on December 3 of that year in Tokyo, Japan. The organization is divided into an executive department and a deliberative department. Chen Qixiu was elected as the director of the executive department, and Yang Donglin was elected as the deputy director. Chen Jinkun was initially elected as the head of the deliberative department, but he resigned and was replaced by Luo Ding. In April of the sixth year of the Republic of China, the inaugural issue of the Arts and Sciences Magazine was published. In May of the seventh year of the Republic of China, students studying in Japan returned to China together to fight for the Sino-Japanese military agreement, and society member Wang Zhaorong was even elected as the leader of the National Salvation Corps. At this time, in addition to maintaining the publication of Arts and Sciences to four thick volumes, other society affairs were temporarily suspended. In the ninth year of the Republic of China, many society members returned to China. In October, the Shanghai office of the society was rented at No. 18, Shunkang Lane, Baotong Road, Shanghai. In December of the eleventh year of the Republic of China, society members held a six-week anniversary meeting in Shanghai, and it was resolved that the Shanghai office would act on behalf of the general office. Zheng Zhenwen was publicly elected as the chief secretary to temporarily act as the general secretary. In June of the twelfth year of the Republic of China, the society charter was revised, and the name was changed to the Chinese Academic Society. In January of the thirteenth year of the Republic of China, Zheng Zhenwen was elected as the first general secretary, and the general office was officially established, and the registration was approved by the Ministry of Education. In that month, Wang Zhaorong and He Songling proposed to筹办筹办 the Academic and Art Institute. After a resolution by the General Office's executive meeting, the Preparatory Committee of the Academic and Art University was organized, and a fundraising committee was organized at the same time to actively proceed. In March, the first annual meeting was held at the Hangzhou Provincial Education Association. In March of the fourteenth year of the Republic of China, the Board of Directors of the Academic and Art University was established, Zheng Zhenwen was elected as the chairman of the board, Wang Zhaorong was elected as the president of the Academic and Art University, and the university charter was passed. No. 320 Jing'an Temple Road was rented as the university campus. In September, the Academic and Art University began to enroll students. In that month, the General Office moved into the Academic and Art University. In October, it was planned to hold the second annual meeting in Wuchang, but the war broke out suddenly, and transportation was cut off. In July of the fifteenth year of the Republic of China, the Academic and Art University's funding was stretched. Also, the charter stipulated that students could not belong to any party or participate in any political activities, which was too restrictive and not suitable for the times. Initially, it was planned to move to Qingdao, but it did not succeed, so it was suspended. In August, the General Office moved to No. 83 Carter Road. In October, the Third Pan-Pacific Science Conference was held. The Society sent Wei Yan籌君 to attend and submit two papers. In November, it was decided that the third annual meeting would be held in Guangzhou in March of the following year, but due to the impact of the current situation and transportation obstruction, the meeting was never held. In September of the sixteenth year of the Republic of China, the General Office moved to No. 35 McLean Lane, North Sichuan Road.

In December of the seventeenth year of the Republic of China, the General Office convened the 12th Anniversary Meeting and the Delegates Assembly from all over the country. In view of the changes in the situation and the many obstacles to progress, the Society discussed the plan to revitalize the Society. After discussion, it was decided to organize a Society Affairs Improvement Committee, and Zhou Jingshou was elected as the chairman. In January of the eighteenth year of the Republic of China, the General Office Construction Committee was established to find land and design plans. On April 1, the Society's charter was revised, changing the executive system to a committee system. In May, the Fourth Pan-Pacific Science Conference was held in Java. Society members Shen Dunhui and Wei Yanshou were elected to represent the Society at the conference, and they all submitted papers. In August, the Executive and Supervisory Committees were established in accordance with the new charter, and Tu Xiaoshi was elected as the chairman of the Executive Committee, and Jing Jing was elected as the chairman of the Supervisory Committee. In October, society members Mao Yike and Hu Jue were elected to attend the International Industrial Conference. In April of the nineteenth year of the Republic of China, Tu Xiaoshi, chairman of the Executive Committee, left Shanghai and was replaced by Fu Shishuo. In December, the fourth annual meeting was held in Nanjing. In January of the twentieth year of the Republic of China, in accordance with the resolution of the fourth annual meeting, Nanjing Academic and Art Middle School was筹办筹办. The construction of the Society's headquarters on Aimei Road, Shanghai, also began in this month. In April, at the request of the Ministry of Industry, society members Tang Gu and Lu Zhihong were elected to attend the Industrial Standards Committee. In January of the twenty-first year of the Republic of China, the Japanese army invaded Shanghai, and the Society's headquarters on McLean Lane, North Sichuan Road, fell into the war zone, and the Society's affairs almost came to a standstill. In March, the Board of Directors was established in accordance with the new charter, Fu Shishuo was elected as the chairman of the Board of Directors, and Bai Pengfei was hired as the director of the General Affairs Department, and Zhou Changshou was hired as the director of the Editorial Department. In May, the new Society headquarters was completed. In June, Nanjing Academic and Art Middle School was established. In August, Luo Zonglu acted as the director of the General Affairs Department, and Zhou Xianwen succeeded as the director of the Editorial Department. In July of the twenty-second year of the Republic of China, Liu Zhuangcai was appointed as the director of the General Affairs Department. In August, the Society's headquarters in Fujian was completed. In February of the twenty-third year of the Republic of China, the Personnel Consulting Office was established, and Pan Gongzhan was hired as the chairman of the committee. In April, the fifth annual meeting was held in Peiping, and it was resolved to revise the Society's charter. In December, the Board of Directors was established in accordance with the charter. In January of the twenty-fourth year of the Republic of China, He Bingsong was elected as the chairman of the Board of Directors. In accordance with the new charter, the Board of Directors hired Chen Qicai, Cai Yuanpei and other twenty-seven people as directors. In February, the Board of Directors was established, and Chen Qicai was elected as the chairman of the Board of Directors. The Board of Directors also hired Liu Zhuang as the general secretary. In April, the sixth annual meeting was held in Wuchang. In May, the Institute of Chinese Studies was established. In October, Liu Zhuang resigned as the general secretary and was succeeded by Zhou Xianwen. In July of the twenty-fifth year of the Republic of China, the seventh annual meeting was held in Nanchang. This is a brief overview of the Society's activities over the past twenty years. As for the Society's more successful publishing business over the past twenty years, it is omitted because there is a special article recording it.

Reflections on the 20th Anniversary of the Chinese Academic Society 179

— Wang Zhaorong

Since the establishment of the Chinese Academic Society, it has been twenty years. During this period, people and things have changed, and the severity of the national crisis has increased, which could not have been imagined when the society was established. It is difficult for scholars to serve the country, and the effect is minimal. Looking back on the past, I am ashamed.

In these twenty years, what the society has presented to the world are: magazines, compilations, collections of papers, various series of books, and photoprinted ancient books. The number of publications is indeed not small. However, other undertakings related to science and art have either failed to proceed due to various reasons, or have proceeded but have not yet shown significant results. This is what we deeply regret. However, the creation of an academic group is very different from the growth of one person, and its lifespan should be calculated in hundreds or thousands of years, and it is definitely not like ordinary people who have the feeling of "how many years does a person live?" Therefore, the society, which is twenty years old, is more appropriately described as still having immaturity and still needs support. However, at the beginning of the establishment of the society, it declared its meaning as: studying truth, promoting academics, exchanging knowledge, and promoting culture. We have adhered to this original intention from beginning to end, hoping to contribute to the country and society through culture and academics.

This kind of cultural undertaking cannot be measured by quick success, but it cannot be stopped for a day. We remember the difficulty of creation, feel the lightness of responsibility, and should always be vigilant and introspect ourselves. If there is progress, we will seek to continue to improve. If there is no success, we must work hard to strive for it. For example, merchants keep daily accounts, monthly settlements, and annual settlements to see their profits and losses. Only by not being complacent can we expect progress. In the past twenty years, although various events have caused the society's affairs to be on the verge of suspension three times, the society has been able to overcome difficulties with the hard work of its members and the assistance of all sectors of society. In the future, if we work hard, we expect that the society's facilities may be different from today in ten or twenty years. The key is that we must not be lazy or complacent, and we must persevere. (Omission)

Furthermore, the 20th anniversary of the society coincides with a time of tension. The borders are threatened, and the country is facing many difficulties. Those who are fighting to defend the country are fighting in the ice and snow. Although we are far away in the rear and our paths are different, our minds are the same. How to contribute to the country is a goal that we must always keep in mind. Different paths lead to the same goal, and we are willing to encourage each other with the people of the country.

Popular Lectures

The Savior Hero of Rome 180

— Li Su

Three brave warriors saved Rome from near destruction

(I) On the Walls of Rome

(Senators stood on the city walls, watching the riverbank opposite, seeing the enemy army under the leadership of Lars Porsena advancing towards Rome. The attacking forces had only one way to approach Rome, and that was a narrow path spanning the river.)

Roman A: We must decide on a strategy immediately to ensure the safety of Rome.

B: Our soldiers are retreating again. With our small army, outnumbered, can we be so lucky?

C: If they can safely retreat across the bridge to this side before the enemy arrives, they will have an excellent opportunity.

B: The most important thing is to act immediately, otherwise, we are finished.

C: I propose that our soldiers cross the bridge as soon as they arrive. Once they have all crossed, we can break the bridge, preventing the enemy from catching up.

A: That seems easy, but who is brave enough to stay on the riverbank and resist the enemy, until the bridge is broken?

B: Roman compatriots, look across the river! The enemy has defeated our troops again. Whatever we do, we must do it immediately.

C: Perhaps Horatius will come and give us an idea.

B: Horatius, today is truly a critical day for the survival of Rome. The enemy could invade the city before nightfall unless we take strong measures immediately.

Horatius: I have discussed with my soldiers, and we all believe that there is only one way to save Rome. That bridge must be destroyed.

B: That's exactly what we thought. But how can this be achieved? Unless we leave some men on that side of the bridge to block the enemy's advance.

Horatius: That narrow bridge, three men are enough to resist a hundred enemy soldiers.

A: That is true, but those three men are as good as dead. Where are we going to find three such brave men to confront the entire enemy army?

Horatius: "Death" will come to everyone in this world, sooner or later, and is there a death more glorious than dying for Rome? I am willing to be one of the three. I believe I can find two more comrades.

C: Well said, Horatius!

Horatius: (To his soldiers). I need two men to go with me to block the enemy while this side dismantles the bridge. It will be a hard fight, perhaps a long one. We may not survive. Who is willing to go?

(Two soldiers step forward).

Soldier: I, Spurius Lartius, am determined to follow you.

Horatius: Thank you, Spurius Lartius. You are a brave man and a strong warrior. I know for sure that you can fight a thousand.

Soldier: And I, Titus Herminius, am determined to follow you.

Horatius: Good! With two such soldiers, one on my left and one on my right, the enemy will not be able to reach the bridge without a long fight.

B: Warriors, we in the rear cannot express our gratitude enough. You are heroes who sacrifice your lives to save Rome.

Horatius: We sacrifice for the love of our country and to give freedom to our descendants. We do not want thanks. Come, Spurius Lartius and Titus Herminius. We have fought hard together with the enemy many times, and I am so lucky to be able to be with you two for the last time. Before the enemy arrives, we must first go and hold our position.

(II) The Bridge

(The Roman army has crossed the bridge and entered the city gate, only those dismantling the bridge have not entered, and the dismantling work is almost complete. Horatius and his two soldiers bravely fought to keep the enemy from setting foot on the bridgehead.)

Horatius: The enemy has retreated to plan a new offensive strategy, Titus Herminius. We must take this opportunity to rest.

Titus: Horatius, did you see them laugh when they first saw us? They aren't laughing now!

Spurius: Be careful, they're coming again!

Titus: Then come on! Let's get close to you. They dare not come forward to meet our sword.

Spurius: Dare not, of course they dare not. Look at the corpses in front of us. I am really very tired. If they attack again in large numbers, I dare not guarantee that I can hold on. Are you injured, Titus Herminius? Why are you using your left hand to hold your sword?

Titus: My right hand is injured, but it doesn't matter. Be quiet, Spurius Lartius! Can you hear them calling us from the end of the bridge? What are they saying?

Horatius: Go back, Titus Herminius! Go back, Spurius Lartius, while the bridge is still standing! Go now, friends, before the enemy returns to attack. I will follow you.

Titus: Come on, Spurius Lartius, now is the time!

(The two of them ran over just before the bridge collapsed. Horatius was able to block the enemy because he stayed behind, when his friends retreated. He retreated step by step to the bridge that had fallen into the river.)

(III) The Riverbank on the Edge of Rome

Titus: Stop, Spurius Lartius - we left Horatius alone. Alas, why didn't he follow us immediately?

Spurius: We can't help him now. He needs our help, Titus Herminius; you see the enemy has forced him back!

Titus: Spurius Lartius, that last sword wounded his face very badly. I'm afraid he's lost an eye.

Spurius: What a brilliant warrior! His sword is broken, but he continues to fight.

Titus: I understand what he is doing. He is resisting until he has a chance to jump into the river.

Spurius: He jumped into the river! Well done, Horatius, he would rather kill himself than fall into the hands of the enemy. Titus Herminius, he is too badly injured to reach our bank.

Titus: You are wrong, Spurius Lartius, you are wrong! He is still fighting, fighting the water for his own life!

Spurius: He's almost to the shore! Work hard, Horatius, come this way! The water is carrying him to our bank.

Titus: Come on, Spurius Lartius, let's help him. He must be almost dead.

(They went out into the water and helped Horatius to the bank.)

Spurius: Hey, brave Horatius, if we didn't think you were following us closely behind, we would never have left you.

Horatius: Friends, please help me. I can't see very clearly. We saved Rome today, and we are still alive to fight for it again

Titus: Come into the city, Horatius. The people are calling for you. The senators have seen everything that has happened on the city walls. They must want to thank you, because you have accomplished what they thought was impossible and saved Rome.

Horatius: I'm not a speaker, Titus Herminius, I'm just a soldier. Take me to a place where I can rest. I am very tired. Titus Herminius and Spurius Lartius, you fought so bravely by my side today that I will never forget it.

Shi Kefa 181

— Zhou Yuan

Heroes cannot be judged by victory or defeat; soldiers who defend their territory and are willing to die with the city are heroes.

When the news of Emperor Sizong of Ming's suicide reached Nanjing, the ministers in Nanjing were so panicked that they couldn't speak; they put on white clothes to mourn Sizong, and tried to send troops to avenge him. They believed that a country cannot be without a ruler for a day, and an emperor must first be established before a vow to launch a northern expedition can be justified; so they immediately discussed the "issue of candidates".

At that time, many princes from Beijing had fled to the south. The most notable were Prince Lu Changfang, who lived in Huai'an, and Prince Fu Zhu Yousong. Ministers Zhang Shenyan, Jiang Yueguang, and others said: "Prince Fu is Emperor Sizong's cousin, so he should be established. But he has many shortcomings, such as being greedy, lustful, unfilial, unwilling to read, mistreating servants, and liking to interfere in other people's affairs. Although Prince Lu is Emperor Sizong's uncle, he is very shrewd and capable, and can be established." At the time, everyone had no objection. However, Ma Shiying, the governor of Fengyang, who had heavy troops, wanted to exploit Prince Fu's shortcomings in order to monopolize power in the court, so he sent troops to send Prince Fu to Yizhen, and the ministers in Nanjing had no choice but to welcome him!

Among these many ministers was a Henan native named Shi Kefa. He was short, with a dark complexion and bright, spirited eyes. When the ministers paid homage to Prince Fu, Prince Fu's face was flushed and he wanted to leave. Shi Kefa stopped him and said, "You can't leave. You should sit upright and receive the homage." Afterwards, when the issue of sending troops was discussed, Shi Kefa said: "The prince should wear plain clothes and personally go to the suburbs to inspect the troops, appoint generals, and prepare for a northern expedition, to show the world his determination to avenge the emperor." Prince Fu nodded and said, "Okay, let's do that!" The next day, the ministers established Prince Fu as emperor. Kefa was appointed Minister of Rites, and later changed to Minister of War. Later, he was appointed as the Grand Coordinator of Yangzhou and stationed in Yangzhou to resist the southern invasion of the Qing army.

Although Kefa became the Grand Coordinator, he shared the hardships with the soldiers in the army day and night, never allowing himself to enjoy any special treatment. If the soldiers were not full, he would not eat first; if the soldiers' clothes were not warm, he would never add a piece of clothing to his own. He read official documents late into the night and did not go to sleep; even when he slept, he just lay down in his clothes and dozed off for a while. Once, on New Year's Eve, he was reading official documents until midnight and had not finished. He was already a little tired and wanted to drink some wine to refresh himself. The cook said, "All the good food has been distributed to the soldiers, and there is nothing to go with the wine. Should I make you some more dishes to go with the wine?" Kefa said, "There's no need to bother so much, just bring some salted soybeans." Kefa usually drank a lot and would not get drunk even after drinking several liters; since coming to the military camp, he had not even smelled the aroma of wine. But this time, he drank ten or more bowls in a row, and as he drank, he suddenly thought of Emperor Sizong, and tears burst out like a flood, and he cried loudly. After a while, he was tired and fell asleep on the table.

When dawn broke, the generals gathered outside the gate, but the gate was tightly closed. They had to wait quietly, guessing what was happening. Later, Kefa's personal servant told them the reason; the prefect Ren Minyu said, "It's rare for him to sleep so soundly. Don't wake him up. Quickly tell the watchman to continue striking the fourth watch. You must all be careful not to make any noise." After a while, Shi Kefa woke up, and the sunlight was already shining brightly through the window. The fourth watch was still being struck outside, and Kefa was furious, shouting, "Who dares to disrupt my laws? Quickly arrest the watchman and kill him!" Ren Minyu quickly came to apologize and explained the intention of the instructions, and he did not kill the watchman. Although his military orders were so strict, he often went to the military camp to talk to the soldiers and personally taught them the methods of attack and defense in battle. If a soldier was sick, he would stroke the patient's wounds and ask in detail about the condition of the illness. Sometimes, when he saw a critically ill person about to die, his eyes would fill with tears and he would choke up and be unable to speak. Therefore, the soldiers often said, "Lord Shi is always thinking about us and cherishing us, how can we not fight hard!"

In the second year of Shunzhi (1645 AD), the Qing government's army, led by Prince Yu Duoduo, marched east from Shaanxi, directly back to Guide in Henan Province. More than 30 counties along the way surrendered at the mere sight of them. After the loss of Guide, they invaded Sizhou in Anhui Province. Shi Kefa was planning to send troops to assist Sizhou in resisting the enemy, but unexpectedly encountered Ningnan Marquis Zuo Liangyu of Ming, who attacked Nanjing in the name of killing the powerful officials Ma Shiying and Ruan Dacheng. The Ming government was extremely frightened and ordered Shi Kefa to rush to Nanjing to rescue it. He had no choice but to change his course to Nanjing. Just as he crossed the river to Yanziji, Zuo Liangyu's army had already been defeated. The Ming government wanted him to hold Siyang, so he hurried back to Tianchang and ordered the generals to rescue Gantai. In the midst of the chaos, a scout reported, "Xutai has already surrendered to the Qing army, and the entire army of Hou Fangyu, the general who was supposed to rescue Sizhou, has been wiped out." Upon hearing this report, he was stunned for a long time, and immediately spent a day and a night rushing back to Yangzhou. His eyes filled with tears, he advised the generals to do their best to defend the territory for the country, and at the same time issued a declaration to the various garrisons to send troops to rescue them.

Who knew that the garrisons would not pay attention to him at all? Only General Liu Xixian led 4,000 soldiers, panting, from Baiyanghe, west of Siyang. He asked Shi Kefa to take advantage of the fact that the Qing soldiers had not yet fully arrived and launch a battle against the city to blunt the enemy's momentum. Shi Kefa did not agree with his opinion, saying, "Rather than fighting in the field, it is better to leave some troops to defend the city and wait for reinforcements from various places." He sent troops to defend the city on the one hand, and sent official documents to the government asking for reinforcements to be dispatched quickly on the other.

On April 20th, the Qing army had all arrived under the city of Yangzhou, stationed at Banzhuyuan. Li Yuchun, a general who had surrendered, brought Prince Yu's letter of surrender and came to the city to persuade them to surrender. Shi Kefa was very angry when he heard that Li Yuchun had come. He walked to the top of the city and scolded Li Yuchun: "The Ming government did not treat you badly, but you have betrayed your kindness and righteousness and surrendered to the Manchus; what face do you have to see me here?" Yuchun, with a thick face, advised him: "Your loyalty and dedication are known to everyone, both at home and abroad. Don't your friends trust you? But now that treacherous officials are in power, what use is it for you to work hard for them? I think it would be better for you to surrender to the Great Qing. Otherwise, even if you sacrifice your life, the Ming government will not give you any benefits! So I advise you to be a peacemaker, so that the two families can stop fighting, and you can also have high positions and high salaries, and your wife and children can be ennobled. Wouldn't that be a win-win situation?" Kefa was furious and said, "Bah! What nonsense are you talking about! Soldiers, quickly shoot this traitor to death with arrows." The arrows on the city all left the strings and flew towards Li Yuchun. Li Yuchun saw that it was not good and galloped away, but because he ran fast, he managed to escape.

After a while, Duoduo called a villager and sent a letter to the moat, asking the guards to explain that he wanted to meet Grand Coordinator Shi. The guards of the moat reported to Shi Kefa, and Kefa lowered a strong soldier from the city and threw the villager and the letter into the water.

Duoduo knew that Shi Kefa loved his country sincerely and respected him very much; the more he respected him, the more he wanted him to surrender. So he ordered the generals to temporarily not attack the city and wrote a tactful letter to Kefa, advising him to surrender. Kefa, upon seeing it, also resolutely rejected it. He threw the letter into the fire to be burned. Prince Yu knew that Kefa's heart could not be moved by words, so he gave the order to attack the city again.

The next day, Gao Qifeng, the supervising vice envoy, and others left the city and surrendered to the Manchus, and the military strength in the city became even weaker. The people's hearts were uneasy, and the civil and military officials in the court all personally went to the city to guard it. At this time, Shi Kefa wrote a letter to his mother and wife, saying goodbye to them. He also calmly instructed his general Shi Dewei: "If I die, please bury my body next to Emperor Gao's Mausoleum. If that is not possible, then bury it under Plum Blossom Ridge!" After saying that, he put on his armor and rushed to the most dangerous West Gate of the old city to defend it.

The more firmly the city was defended, the more fierce the attack became. The Qing soldiers besieged Yangzhou so tightly that no water could escape, attacking day and night. Shi Kefa was anxious. He attacked the enemy with cannons, killing several thousand people. Seeing this situation, the commander-in-chief of the Qing army personally led a death squad to attack the city. Suddenly, a loud noise like thunder exploded in the northwest corner of the city, and it collapsed. The Qing soldiers took advantage of the gap and rushed in. The Ming soldiers defending the city did not show weakness and stood firm, desperately firing arrows at the people climbing the city. The corpses under the city piled up like a mountain; the enemy soldiers stepped on these corpses one by one and ascended the city. Thus, the flags of the Manchus were raised on the city.

When the city was under heavy siege, Shi Kefa said to Zhuang Zigu: "If the city is broken, please kill me with your sword first." Zhuang Zigu also agreed. At this time, Shi Kefa stretched out his neck and asked Zigu to cut it. How could Zigu bear to do it? Seeing that he was unwilling, Kefa immediately drew his sword and slashed at his own neck. Zigu was shocked and rushed forward to hug him, snatching the sword from his hand. Although he did not die, his clothes were already stained with red blood.

At that time, Zigu and dozens of others dragged and carried Kefa out of the city. Just as they reached the Little East Gate, the Qing soldiers saw many Ming soldiers walking out of the city and fired arrows at them; Zigu, Xu Jin, and others were all shot to death. Kefa struggled with his injuries and shouted in a loud voice, "I am Grand Coordinator Shi of this city, you can just take me to see your commander-in-chief!" These Qing soldiers were a little disbelieving when they heard that it was Grand Coordinator Shi, but they did not dare to underestimate him; they dragged and pulled him to the South Gate Tower of the new city to see Duoduo.

Duoduo was in the midst of chaos when he saw the soldiers lead in a bloody Ming person. He was very surprised and asked, "Who are you?" Shi Kefa answered calmly, "I am Shi Kefa." Duoduo was surprised that it was Shi Kefa and could not speak for a long time, staring at him with his eyes wide open. After a while, he said, "I admire you very much for defending the isolated city alone. Now that the city has been broken, your loyalty and effort to your country can be considered exhausted. Can you agree to my request and unify Jiangnan for our Qing government?" When Kefa heard that he wanted him to surrender, he pointed his hair at the sky and said loudly, "I am a minister of the Ming Dynasty. The imperial court gave me Yangzhou, but I failed to defend it for him; what face do I have to live in dishonor? Now that I have come here, I only want to borrow your sword to take off my head. I have no other intention, do not misunderstand me." Although Duoduo saw that he spoke with certainty, he still did not give up and said, "Have you not seen our Grand General Hong Chengchou? If you are willing to work for us, you can receive the same benefits as him." Shi Kefa smiled contemptuously and said, "Humph, Hong Chengchou? Can you treat Hong Chengchou better than Emperor Chongzhen treated him? He received so much grace from the imperial court, but he betrayed the imperial court; can he really be loyal to you? I am always ashamed of his treason and hate his lack of conscience; would I go and learn from him?" Prince Yu had nothing to say, but he thought that he was in a fit of rage and that it would naturally not be successful to persuade him to surrender. So he ordered one of his most eloquent generals, named Yierdun, to accompany him and slowly persuade him to surrender, hoping to move his heart.

Yierdun accompanied Kefa for three days and persuaded him for three whole days, but Shi Kefa still refused to surrender. Duoduo knew that Kefa's patriotic loyalty was as strong as iron and could not be shaken, and he was afraid that keeping him would be detrimental to his country. Therefore, Kefa died for his country at their hands.

The Publishing Industry

Reading Guidance, Series 2 183

— Bin

——Published by The Commercial Press——

In recent years, the publishing industry in our country has been very enthusiastic about promoting reading, and reading magazines, reading guides, college entrance examination guides, and books on various subject guides and research methods have sprung up like mushrooms; this is certainly a good phenomenon. However, if we examine this type of book strictly, we will feel dissatisfied; either the editors and authors are sloppy, or the content is repetitive and uninspired. Therefore, supplying students, readers, and researchers with this type of crudely made books will probably be counterproductive to the original intention of the publishers, and will also have great harm to them. At the same time, it will greatly hinder the progress of the reading movement; for this matter, publishers and editors cannot shirk responsibility. While feeling disappointed, we still hope that the publishing industry can publish some good books, such as reading guides, for readers to read.

In the expectations of most readers, The Commercial Press's reading guides have been published one after another; this is certainly a very gratifying thing. The first series of the book has been published for a year, and it is said to be quite popular and well-received by readers. The second series was published only recently, so we think it is necessary to introduce and comment on it. The articles included in Reading Guidance, Series 2, are divided into a total of fifteen categories, totaling thirty-one articles; some of them were not included in the first series, which can be said to have fulfilled the task of supplementing it.

Mr. Cai Yuanpei once pointed out in the preface of the book the advantages that a book of reading guidance should have, namely: "convenient for self-study", "convenient for reference", and "convenient for increasing common sense". Reading Guidance, Series 2, contains these three advantages. The thirty-one articles included in it either contain one of the above advantages, or have two or even all of them. Now, let us cite these articles and add a brief comment; from this, we can imagine how suitable the content of the entire series of articles is for the needs of readers.

First, there is Ma Zongrong's How to Study Library Science? In this short article, he expresses his opinions on the importance of studying library science and experience, and introduces many good books on library science for beginners. This can be said to be a suitable path for them.

Second, there is Zhou Yutong's How to Study Classics? He advocates that researchers should first understand classics before talking about research; and they must have a foundation in philology before research can be carried out without difficulty. He has a special insight into the interpretation and classification of classics. As for how to read classics, he advocates that one should first read simple classics books, and then read problematic and important ones. The final conclusion is this: "To study the classics with the viewpoint of 'history', and to excavate the buried materials in the classics with the viewpoint of social science." This is certainly more novel and applicable than the opinions of some stubborn scholars of the classics.

Books and Periodicals - A Review 184

The Crisis in the Far East: "The Crisis in the Far East," originally titled "The Far Eastern Crisis I Recollections and Observations," was written by Stimson, the Secretary of State during President Hoover's term. The original book was published in September of this year, and the Shanghai Tianjin Ta Kung Pao began translating and publishing it daily in early October. The entire book consists of approximately 200,000 words, divided into five chapters: 1. The Background of American Far Eastern Policy; 2. Mediation of the Manchurian Crisis; 3. China's Proposals in the League of Nations; 4. Determination of Responsibility; 5. Conclusion. It provides extremely detailed and thorough accounts of the events of September 18th Incident and the January 28th Incident, international diplomatic activities, and America's Far Eastern policy, from John Hay's Open Door Policy and the Washington Conference up to the September 18th Incident. It further analyzes the opening of the war, the exposure of the great powers' secrets, the policies of China and Japan, the development of the crisis, and future disasters. This book is published by Nanjing Zhengzhong Book Company, translated by Cao Mingdao, and priced at seven dimes.

The Persians: If you have a slight knowledge of Greek drama, you will know the famous playwright Aeschylus. "The Persians" is one of his masterpieces. This is a tragedy that takes place in 480 BC, describing the war between Persia and Greece. It portrays how the Persian elders and Empress Dowager worried about the King and soldiers who were on expeditions, especially focusing on the fear that was carved into their hearts. The author focused on psychological description, which was very successful. The entire play is full of the colors of war, and at the same time, it inspires the enthusiasm to resist the enemy and defend the country. This book is published by Commercial Press, translated by Luo Niansheng, and priced at five dimes.

Early Childhood Psychology: Early Childhood Psychology is divided into sixteen chapters. It provides detailed descriptions, discussions, and instructions on topics such as the child's close ancestral heredity, innate reserves, reflexes and aimless activities, instinctive tendencies, emotions, habit formation, the process of thought, the development of social attitudes, imagination, memory, perception and sensation, language and images, individual differences, and special problems in child development. This book is published by Zhonghua Book Company, translated by Zhu Zhensun, and priced at one dollar.

How to Study Philosophy (3) 185

— Yan Yilin

Written by Wang Tefu, published by Sanjiang Bookstore

...in order to sort out some clues, order, and boundaries from the complex philosophical content, so that there is a certain theoretical thread to follow when studying. Only in this way can one understand its theories and viewpoints. This kind of analytical work can be said to be a necessary process of clarification when studying philosophy, so it is said that this kind of analytical work is necessary in philosophical research.

5. Comprehensive Research on Philosophy:

The problems in philosophy are fundamentally related and unified. The overall form of philosophy is a whole worldview and outlook on life, a complete spiritual system, rather than fragmented, unrelated theories and thoughts. Because the various problems in philosophy are organically interrelated, comprehensive research should also be carried out simultaneously with analytical research. Understanding parts and individual problems is just as important as understanding the whole and general problems. If we want to establish a whole worldview and outlook on life, and if we want to understand the whole form of philosophy, then comprehensive research on philosophy is necessary. As for how to conduct comprehensive research, on the one hand, we must start with the synthesis between the parts of the object of philosophy, and from this, proceed to the recognition of the whole truth of the world. Then, the form and content of this synthesis will include the relationship and sum of the various parts and the whole of natural philosophy, social philosophy, and even the science of thinking; on the other hand, we should comprehensively consider the various problems of philosophy itself in order to recognize the whole of philosophy and to have a complete system of philosophical thought. In short, if you do not conduct analytical research, but study philosophy in a superficial way, you cannot understand the specific content of philosophy, and therefore it is not easy to obtain an accurate and precise worldview; but if you only do fragmented research, only focus on specific individual problems and ignore the whole picture of philosophy, you still cannot understand the entire philosophical system and obtain the entire worldview. Concrete and detailed research, and systematic and comprehensive research, are research methods that must be used at any time in philosophical research.

The Enlightenment of Sex

— Doctor Zhan Nianceng

The Relationship Between Masturbation and Neurasthenia 188

...Premature ejaculation, impotence, and obstructed genital development are all symptoms induced by excessive masturbation... Masturbation in childhood often jointly inhibits the development and vitality of the testicles and prostate.

Masturbation is harmful and not beneficial to young people, which is a fact well known to people who know a little medical common sense. However, at what time does this behavior begin to have the most harmful effect? From the perspective of physical constitution, first of all, it is the most obvious in people with the nervous system. In addition, people with adenoid constitution are subject to a relatively large impact. This is because the nervous system is too sensitive and its resistance is too weak.

Supplement to the Shanghai Newspaper

Small Talk

The So-Called "Nation-Protecting Disaster-Relieving Dharma Assembly" 196

— Shi Ji

After the alarming news of the Suiyuan border crisis arrived, calls for aid to Suiyuan resounded throughout the land. The inspiring and moving stories within this are simply too numerous to record. For example, the widowed woman of Cixi who emptied her family's coffers to alleviate the disaster is one example; the students of Beiping who, defying the municipal government's accusations of disrupting order, continued their aid Suiyuan movement, is another example; the elementary school students of Wuhu who, while raising funds for aid to Suiyuan, were inexplicably beaten severely, is yet another example; as for the common laborers and peddlers, who are usually looked down upon by the gentry, who were willing to go hungry and suffer more from the cold to save a few copper coins to express their heartfelt intentions, that is an even more widespread occurrence. The Chinese nation will never perish, and these instances not only give us a glimpse of hope but also provide us with a guarantee!

However, amidst the nationwide rise of calls to save the country, some gentry are playing the trick of the so-called "Nation-Protecting Disaster-Relieving Dharma Assembly." The "Nation-Protecting Disaster-Relieving Dharma Assembly" was initiated before the bandit-puppet regime invaded Suiyuan. At that time, the situation in Hebei and Chahar was very urgent, and "protecting the nation" was indeed a matter of utmost importance. As for "relieving disaster," although there was a harvest in various places this year, the malignant malaria around Gaoyou was extremely rampant, and whether the farmers could live and work in peace after the harvest was indeed quite questionable. At this time, holding a Dharma Assembly that both "protects the nation" and "relieves disaster" is naturally very timely.

Moreover, it is said that the good harvests in various places this year are due to the fact that a Bingzi Disaster-Relieving Dharma Assembly was held not long ago, which is why there is now an abundant harvest of crops. Abundant harvest is a fact; the so-called Bingzi Disaster-Relieving Dharma Assembly was indeed held not long ago; therefore, if the two are linked together as cause and effect, then one can only defer to that opinion. But it also makes us think of other things. If we were not as forgetful as those "lay Buddhists" and "Dharma Masters," I think we would definitely be able to remember. Let's take an example! For example, the Vajra Wheel Dharma Assembly, which was even more grand than the Bingzi Disaster-Relieving Dharma Assembly, and presided over by a Living Buddha, the magnificence of which has not yet been forgotten by us. However, this grand Dharma Assembly took place several years ago, and in these years, China is still facing a "serious national crisis." Not only "serious," but now it should be written that the national crisis is increasingly urgent.

But even though the "national crisis is increasingly urgent," the various Dharma Assemblies initiated by the gentry are endlessly emerging with ever-changing tricks. This time, the new banner being raised is called the "Nation-Protecting Disaster-Relieving Dharma Assembly," which happens to coincide with the bandit-puppet regime's invasion of Suiyuan, and thanks to the loyalty and bravery of the soldiers and the spiritual and material assistance of the people in the rear, a victory was won.

The victory and the "Nation-Protecting Disaster-Relieving Dharma Assembly" are linked together, and the "Nation-Protecting Disaster-Relieving Dharma Assembly" naturally has immense merit. But just as I was thinking this way, I saw a sketch about the assembly in a newspaper:

'...When they entered a room filled with many longevity tablets, the Dharma Master widened his Dharma eyes and stared intently at the tablets, chanting mantras. According to a monk from the temple, these longevity tablets are priced at two yuan and ten yuan each. People who spend money to buy these tablets can eliminate disasters and prolong their lives as long as the Dharma Master casts his Dharma eyes on their tablet...'

Only then did I suddenly realize that the so-called "Nation-Protecting Disaster-Relieving" is actually such a thing, and under such "protection" and "relief," the most important thing is still two yuan or even ten yuan. As for what is the difference between two yuan and ten yuan? Unfortunately, I am not a "Dharma Master" or "lay Buddhist," and the reporter did not write it out, so there is no way to know. But although the difference between two yuan and ten yuan is unknown, the benefits for the "Dharma Master" and the celebrities who initiated the assembly must be greater than this, I think that is certain. Otherwise, wouldn't the enthusiastic efforts be in vain? And wouldn't the frequent construction of Dharma altars be even more superfluous?

"Protecting the nation" is a good topic, and "relieving disaster" is also a good topic, as we struggle to survive under frequent disasters year after year. And to be able to eliminate disasters and prolong life by spending two yuan is an extremely cheap "good deed." It is no wonder that there are many believers when the Dharma Assembly is held. One can imagine the joyous faces of the initiating celebrities and the presiding Dharma Master when they see so many longevity tablets, that expression must be quite interesting. Don't say disappointing things when encountering successful people, I understand this worldly wisdom. At this time, if one were to talk about benefiting others and benefiting oneself, the small self and the great self, it would be too insensitive; since there is nothing to say, I might as well put down the pen here.

Salt Fields 197

— Lu Zhi

As we walked towards the seaside, thick fog enveloped us. It was wet, salty, and like a fine drizzle. The fog rolled onto the embankment in gusts, coming from who knows where, and going to who knows where, a blanket of white. The sun was like a white porcelain lamp floating in the fog.

On the embankment, there was only Zheng Bao and I. We were both tired of walking. Along the way, we passed through many brine pits, salt-boiling sheds, and villages, encountering many little girls and children crossing the embankment, carrying bamboo strips to collect clams. After walking a long time, we turned a corner and finally arrived at Zheng Bao's relative's house.

As we entered the sparse village, several dogs surrounded us and barked. We knocked on the door for a long time, but only the dogs barked.

Zheng Bao, afraid that I would be anxious, said, "They won't be out this early." In fact, we were both tired of walking and wanted to rest. Since we couldn't find anyone, we were both a little annoyed.

"Oh, Zheng Bao, is that you... Get away, get away, kill you (speaking to the dogs). We thought it was someone else, you really scared us!" Two elderly men dressed as farmers came out from next door, one of whom said enthusiastically.

"Is this Xu Fuguan's house?" Zheng Bao asked urgently.

"He's not home!" The two men looked at me, filled with suspicion.

"This is my friend. Because he wants to visit Zhapu and see how salt is made, I came to find Fuguan with him."

The two men didn't reply, and quietly led us through the back door into the house. All the way, we chased away the dogs that were following us.

"Fuguan went out so early? Where's his mother? Where's his sister-in-law?" Zheng Bao asked.

"Ha... Ha... (bitterly laughed) They're boiling salt right now. They ran out of salt for cooking, and they wanted to take advantage of the heavy fog, so no one could see the smoke, to boil some for themselves. They usually don't dare to... I didn't expect you to come, wearing two coats. We thought you were salt inspectors. When they heard, they all ran away."

"Ran away?" We both unconsciously repeated.

"You sit for a while, we'll go find them."

Sitting in the room, which was both a kitchen and a living room, although the light was very dim, and the musty smell hit my nose in waves, I felt as settled as if I were at home. We both didn't say anything, looking at the unplastered walls, on which were two comical and rough paintings of "Fighting the Japanese." Beside the stove was a large bamboo cupboard, all dilapidated, as if it would break apart at the slightest touch. This family is still a good family, I really don't trust what Zheng Bao said.

Tired of sitting, we turned out the back door and walked closer to the bamboo garden. Suddenly, we saw smoke and steam rising over there. An iron pan, two feet square, was overturned on the ground. Under the pan was a square stove made of stones, and there was still a fire burning.

"This is the salt they're boiling!" I said, as if I had discovered a secret.

"How many pounds do you think they can boil here?" Zheng Bao asked me maturely.

"Two or three pounds!" I said.

At this moment, I heard hurried footsteps, and a thin man with a purplish face, nearly thirty years old, ran in.

"Oh, Brother Dou, what wind blew you here?... You scared me, it's really like 'you don't steal for a thousand days, but you get caught the moment you do'... Oh, this gentleman, please come in and sit, it's too dirty here."

We sat down, and he hurriedly fetched water, started the fire, and brewed tea for us to drink. "Did you come on the second bus? You should have come on the early bus, we wouldn't have been suspicious so early."

I felt sorry that I had caused this honest man such a scare. I was also curious as to why they were so afraid. "Can't you even boil this little bit to eat?"

"No, even half a catty will be fined three or four dollars! That's the rule." He said with a smile, revealing a mouthful of yellowed and uneven teeth. He was still panting.

"What if you can't pay the fine?" I asked, and then scolded myself for being too stupid.

"What else but getting beaten and going to jail." He sighed.

"Don't they boil salt now?" Zheng Bao asked. "He wanted to see how salt is boiled."

"Not allowed to boil it now, the public warehouse has too much salt stored. They're afraid of people boiling it privately."

The tea was brewed, like yellow mud, with a salty taste. Just as I was holding the teacup, two women stumbled in through the back door, one with bound feet only three inches long, and the other with large feet wearing cloth shoes, with mud splashing all the way up to their thighs. When they saw Zheng Bao, they forced a smile and said, "Bao, what wind blew you here? Look at your aunt and your sister-in-law, we've turned into two mud bodhisattvas... I fell three times."

The chair I was sitting on felt like it had thorns, and I couldn't settle down. I borrowed the excuse of going to Haiyan, and I pulled Zheng Bao away from this kind family. We didn't say a word on the way.

Old Theories and New Proofs of "Traitors" 200

— Wen

The meaning of "traitor" is very clear, no need to elaborate, it is someone who betrays the country. However, in certain situations, there are also cases where, depending on the viewer, a traitor is seen as not a traitor, and a non-traitor is seen as a traitor. For example, going to Changchun or eastern Hebei to shout about saving the country will definitely be regarded as a "spy" without a doubt, and nothing but killing or arrest will do. This is clear proof. Thus, the meaning of "traitor" needs to be explained in more detail.

Flipping through my hand, I have a copy of the fourth issue of "Zhong Liu" magazine, which contains an article by Mr. Zheng Zhenduo called "Notes on Selected Texts." In his selection of late Qing dynasty texts, he discovered an article called "Distinguishing Traitors" by an unknown author, which was published in the late Qing dynasty secret revolutionary publication "Yellow Emperor's Soul." This provides a very detailed explanation of the definition of a traitor. In today's world where it is difficult to distinguish between black and white, re-publishing this article has great significance. Therefore, without avoiding repetition, I will transcribe it below:

The so-called true traitor is one who helps foreign races harm their own race. Guan Gan, who taught the Jin to advance; Zhang Tuo, who helped Shi Le destroy the Jin; Shi Jingtang, who served the Khitans as his father; Zhao Yanshou, who led dogs and sheep to slaughter their own kind; Zhang Hongfan, who helped the Yuan destroy the Song; Wu Sangui, Geng Jimao, and Shang Kexi, who helped the Qing destroy the Ming; Zeng Guofan, Zuo Zongtang, Li Hongzhang, and others, who helped the Manchus annihilate the Taiping Heavenly Kingdom, are all today's dead traitors... As for what the Manchus called traitors, they were the great men and scholars of the Han race, who were willing to submit to foreign rulers for the sake of loving their own kind, even sacrificing themselves without hesitation, such as Huo Qubing and Wei Qing, who killed the Xiongnu during the reign of Emperor Wu of Han; Yue Fei of the Song Dynasty; Hong Xiuquan, the Taiping Heavenly King of modern times; and the martyrs Tang Caichang and Lin Shutang... We respectfully advise the Han people to be careful not to be traitors who harm themselves, but to be traitors who love themselves... Do not allow foreigners to call us traitors, and thus avoid the name of traitor and avoid it. Mr. Zheng noted: "At that time, Manchu officials often gave the title of traitor to revolutionaries, hence the author's explanation." This has made it very clear who the real traitors are, and what a traitor is. The standard for distinguishing is: Who leads dogs and sheep to slaughter their own kind, and who is willing to submit to foreign rulers and sacrifice themselves for the sake of loving their own kind?

The enemy comes with guns and cannons. Everyone can see it. The most terrible thing is: using your Han race to kill your Han race. In the enemy's secret plan, this is called "using Chinese to control Chinese." Aren't the so-called puppet troops who are causing chaos in eastern Suiyuan Chinese people? To expand on this, the enemy's visible and invisible hired executioners are currently numerous. They are killing with enthusiasm, and the enemy is watching from the sidelines and reaping the benefits. The grievances are soaring to the sky, and in the end, it is all their own people who are being killed. Mr. Zheng said in "Notes on Selected Texts," "Some of what they said is still useful today... Reading the articles full of anger and motivating national spirit that they published twenty or thirty years ago, I really can't help but feel that they are not outdated." I say, "It was like this in the past, and it is even more so today!"

I remember not long ago, Chairman Chiang Kai-shek said in his speech at the Luoyang Military Branch School, "To revive the nation, we must first eliminate domestic traitors" (paraphrased). Therefore, I cite old theories to prove new events.

Candy 201

— Tianshe

Because of the constant pain from a few decayed teeth, I have finally become less fond of sweet things. Even the noble chocolates and fashionable spearmint gums have become mere toys to me. The brocade box with the seven-colored rubber stamp, the American pastoral scene seen through the cellophane on the box, a group of lively and innocent children chasing turkeys on a farm, a clothes rack in front of a clapboard house, a two-horse carriage in the distance, a middle-aged farmer smoking tobacco, and the sunshine on horseback... A rainbow-like, wheat-colored or lake-green ribbon diagonally crossed the picture, tightly tied in a bow on the corner of the brocade box. The simple color of the chocolate is pleasing to me.

This time, among the farewell gifts that Dai An gave me, there was such a box, "noble toy." Oh, a sorrow of the appetite quietly arises from within. There is some bitterness in the sweetness of the chocolate, is it the bitterness that can tempt my appetite, or is it the charred aroma that is tasted from the hidden? Over the years, the tempering of my heart and life has been stained with the color and taste of chocolate, a kind of ochre simplicity, a kind of bitter charred aroma, tightly making me linger, while the sweetness has finally become less appealing to me, this should be blamed on my past overeating of sugar, which ruined my teeth.

When I got home, I distributed the candy to the children, and only kept the brocade box for myself. However, when the children peeled open the shiny tin foil and saw the hard piece, they stared with their little round eyes in confusion; "What is this? There's no sesame and roses." Children living in the countryside have always been isolated from the material civilization of the city. What is considered a precious item in the city only earns a little doubt and contempt in the countryside. Just like wearing a suit to the countryside and being scolded as a monkey, even if my heart is filled with some indignation and grievances, I have to silently endure it. In the countryside, the status of sesame candy is much better than chocolate.

When the afternoon sun shines directly on the lonely courtyard, there will be a hoarse, seemingly laborious peddling sound, accompanied by the sound of iron pieces striking each other, unexpectedly breaking into the village lanes. It is very familiar, even for a traveler like me who rarely returns, I know that the old man selling sesame candy is here again. "Buy sesame candy, exchange rotten things for sesame candy, rose-salted sesame candy!" It lures some children out of the high and low doorways. The old man and his candy stall are surrounded in front of the ancestral hall's screen wall. He has a thin triangular face, moist eyes with fixed, dull pupils, a long neck, exposing two thick veins. When he raises his head and shouts, the thick veins turn purple, the purple of blood.

Sesame candies are stacked one by one in the tray, very neatly. The tray is placed on a bamboo basket, in which are randomly thrown some rags and rotten cotton. Most of his life is found in the wreckage. The remnants of life abandoned by others are becoming the only source of his life.

My little nephews pulled at the corner of my clothes, dragging me to the candy stall, pointing to the sesame candy in the tray. I had already discerned their little intentions. The old man smiled at me strangely, frequently throwing his hopeful gaze at me. I don't know how many years it has been since I traded with a candy vendor in my hometown, haven't eaten the crispy sesame candy of my hometown, haven't fooled around with many companions with the candy vendor. Although these situations are far apart in time, from the hazy memories, I seemed to return to my lost childhood. My teeth don't seem to be decayed, my third uncle, who often bought candy for me, is still healthy and alive, I can still distinguish the taste of salted caramel and roses, and I haven't forgotten the anger of my second brother always eating up his share first, and then coming to snatch mine.

But there is no me and my second brother in the current group of children. The spirit tablets of my third uncle have long been enshrined in the wooden niches of the ancestral hall. Many unfamiliar children's faces tell me; this is another generation's life. I stood in front of the candy stall, not knowing whether I was happy or sad? Even my own sense of self suddenly became blurred.

"Uncle, buy. Uncle, buy." The urging of my little nephews woke me up again. I took out copper coins from my pocket, bought a few sesame candies and distributed them. They scurried into the house, jumping and running. "Hehehe... Your husband really likes children." These unexpected words burst out from the old candy seller's dry throat. "Uh..." This nasal answer I suspected was not my own. I watched him put the heavy candy stall on his shoulder, hunching his back, walking step by step, and finally disappearing at the end of the lane, he was going to finish that unfinished road of life.

Returning to the house, I stared blankly at the chocolate brocade box on the table, and the decayed tooth was aching again...

Film

Huaan Broadcasting 206

The radio play "Heroic Woman of a Lonely City" is a collaboration between Zhonghua Tong, recording by Jin Xiangjiu, photography by Chen Chen, set design by Zhang Hanchen, and starring Chen Yanyan, Zheng Junli, and Shang Kouwu.

The entire film "Song of a慈母曲" has been completed, and the results are excellent. However, in order to expand the promotion of this film, although it has been decided to premiere at the Jincheng Theater, the screening date has not yet been easily determined.

Sun Yu's new work "Spring Comes to the World" features a scene of Peach Leaf Bridge, built in the south of the main factory. The water meanders, and the bridge spans both banks. The scenery is entirely in the Suzhou style. If a few soft Wu dialect sounds are added, floating in between, it would be truly like being on the side of Wu Wang Terrace.

The prison scene in "General's Daughter" is grand and gloomy, worthy of being called a masterpiece. It can be compared to foreign films and is designed by the set designer Xu Ke.

Zheng Junli plays Zhang Zhengke, a calm and rational revolutionary in "Heroic Woman of a Lonely City." He is calm and capable, just like his character. His "engaged" but not "married" wife Chen Yanyan is a modest young woman who makes a living by selling pearl rice.

Li Zhuozhuo plays the general's daughter in He Mengfu's "General's Daughter." She is insightful and firmly believes in the Three Principles of the People. She does not condone her father's actions, accepts the party's orders, and puts righteousness before family, acting very movingly.

Han Langan, who had been wandering for many years, suddenly appeared wearing a top hat and a tuxedo, holding a "stick," strutting around. It turned out that he had been re-employed by the factory owner Liu Jiqun as a representative for escorting automobiles. On the day of Han Langan's wedding, the gift from factory owner Liu was a red silk congratulatory banner with the four characters "A Match Made in Heaven" affixed to it. (In Shen Fu's film "A Match Made in Heaven.")

Shirley Temple's New Film "Dimples" 207

Premiering today at the Grand Cathay simultaneously

"Dimples," produced by 20th Century Fox, is Shirley Temple's latest masterpiece. The film tells the story of an orphan with no parents who relies on her unambitious grandfather to eke out a living. Although this grandfather loves his granddaughter very much, he himself is prone to random talking and meddling. Although Shirley tries to persuade him, it's no use, but Shirley's enthusiasm for her grandfather never wanes. Later, although a wealthy woman offers her grandfather thousands of dollars to take Shirley in, Shirley ultimately stops because she can't bear to leave her grandfather. Later, her talent for acting is discovered by a playwright, and she begins a stage life. On the day she goes on stage, her grandfather is about to be arrested because of a past act of deception, but as a result, the plaintiff is moved by her sincere performance and abandons everything. In this film, not only is Shirley's performance skillful, but Frank Morgan, who plays the old grandfather, also has amazing gains. Premieres simultaneously at the Grand Cathay theaters.

Two Songs from "Little Orphan Girl" 208

Xinhua Company's exquisite work "Little Orphan Girl," following "Night of Joy," has been completed and will be screened at the Jincheng Theater after "Life and Death Together." This film is the first starring role for child star Chen Juanjuan, with surprisingly mature acting skills. There are two songs in the film, sung by Chen Juanjuan, which are exceptionally melodious. Little Orphan Girl

(2) The sparrow chirps chirp chirp, parents and siblings are separated by life and death, life and death are imminent, the orphan wanders for thousands of miles.

(3) The cat meows mimi, the orphan can't bear the hunger in her belly, the hunger in her belly, no one cares about three meals a day.

(4) The crow caws gua gua, the orphan is desolate and has no home to return to, no home to return to, spending the long night on the windy and rainy streets.

(2) Sit in a circle, eat fruit, everyone listen to me again, go to bed early when the day is over, cultivate energy, don't be lazy, dad farms the fields, brother does the work, although people are small, there is a lot of strength, don't miss the time, haha ​​hee hee, hee hee haha, we are all old brothers.
